The knowledge model turns that charter into an explicit contract for artifacts, source segments, claims, people or systems, transformation activities, context, rights, status, and relationships, while avoiding the assumption that every form of knowledge can be reduced to one record type (W3C PROV-O, W3C Web Annotation, ISO 23081-1). Provenance should distinguish entities, activities, and agents; derivation and attribution should be explicit; annotations should remain separate objects tied to exact targets or segments; and invalidation or supersession should preserve lifecycle history instead of silently replacing it (W3C PROV-O, W3C Web Annotation, Dublin Core terms). A small purpose-specific application profile can combine reusable descriptive terms, preferred and alternative vocabulary labels, validation constraints, persistent identifiers, provenance, rights, review state, and disposition without forcing one universal ontology or storage technology (Dublin Core terms, W3C SKOS, W3C SHACL, FAIR principles). This model must keep authority, confidence, approval, and truth distinct, because metadata copied into an annotation is not authoritative for the external resource and validation conformance is determined by results rather than successful ingestion alone (W3C Web Annotation, W3C SHACL).

The platform should be a set of replaceable capabilities around canonical content and identifiers, typed metadata and provenance, indexing and retrieval, synchronization and integration, workflow and presentation, and tested export, backup, and recovery (NIST cloud portability, NIST backup guidance, NIST contingency planning). Interoperability concerns exchange with preserved semantics, portability includes both data and workload movement, and resilience depends on demonstrated recovery rather than the presence of an exporter or archive (NIST cloud portability, NIST backup guidance). A representative portable design can use declared-encoding CommonMark for narrative, JSON-LD for structured relationships, stable identifiers, checksums, attachment storage, a transactional database such as SQLite, and rebuildable indexes, while BagIt packages can carry arbitrary payloads with verifiable manifests (CommonMark specification, JSON-LD 1.1, SQLite long-term support, BagIt RFC). Format choice should be judged by disclosure, adoption, transparency, self-documentation, dependencies, patents, protection mechanisms, and the needs of future users, while recovery exercises should test backups and allow limited manual operation where appropriate (Library of Congress format sustainability, NIST backup guidance, NIST contingency planning).

AI context engineering should treat machine memory as a controlled projection of the canonical store rather than a second source of truth, because retrieval-augmented generation combines parametric model memory with external non-parametric memory but does not by itself solve provenance or updating (RAG study). Context selection should seek the smallest sufficient, authorized, current, and attributable evidence set because long-context models use the same relevant information differently depending on position and often use middle-position evidence less effectively (Lost in the Middle). Machine-usable memory should retain source, segment, creator, derivation, time, scope, rights, confidence, version, contradiction, and supersession, while raw conversations remain evidence sources and proposed durable memories require validation before write-through to the canonical model (W3C PROV-O, ICO individual-rights guidance, NIST AI RMF Core). Retrieval should filter permissions, tenant, purpose, recency, and status before ranking, and evaluation should separate extraction, multi-session reasoning, temporal reasoning, updates, abstention, attribution, unauthorized retrieval, and deletion propagation because sustained-interaction memory remains difficult on LongMemEval (LongMemEval, ICO individual-rights guidance). MCP can expose schema-declared tools with human denial capability and requires clients to treat annotations as untrusted unless the server is trusted, while A2A can exchange stateful tasks and typed artifacts across heterogeneous agents without exposing internal memory or tools (MCP tools specification, A2A specification).

The cross-child design tensions are structural rather than defects to eliminate: broad capture increases future option value but also maintenance, privacy, noise, and governance cost; rich metadata improves traceability but raises capture burden; plain files improve transparency while databases improve transactions and query control; synchronization improves availability while rapidly propagating corruption; and long context preserves fidelity while retrieval can omit decisive evidence (FAIR principles, W3C SHACL, NIST backup guidance, Lost in the Middle). Managed cloud services can reduce operational burden but deepen dependence on provider identity, APIs, pricing, and export fidelity, while an open format or checksum does not alone prove semantic portability, truth, security, or restorability (NIST cloud portability, BagIt RFC, Library of Congress format sustainability). The strategy should therefore prefer bounded, reversible, instrumented pilots with explicit knowledge limits, human oversight, risk tolerance, recovery evidence, and exit paths, then carry the same identifiers, provenance, rights, status, and evaluation criteria into capture, organization, validation, retrieval, synthesis, and maintenance across the lifecycle (GOV.UK success guidance, NIST AI RMF Core, NIST backup guidance, W3C PROV-O).

2.1 Purposes, intended outcomes, and success criteria

Start with the user’s problem, not the repository

A second brain should be justified by a recurring user problem and intended outcome rather than by ownership of a repository, adoption of a method, or accumulation of notes (UK service guidance on user needs, UK guidance on defining success). Planning should begin with evidence about who the users are and what they need, and a valid need should describe the problem without presupposing a tool or delivery mechanism (UK service guidance on user needs). Stakeholder assumptions are not an adequate substitute because user needs should be validated through research (UK service guidance on user needs).

The purpose should identify what changes for whom: faster or more accurate completion of a realistic knowledge task, more reliable prospective action, improved learning or unaided capability, or an organizational outcome tied to knowledge use (UK service measurement guidance, reminder study, offloading study, ISO 30401). These purposes require different criteria because external reminders can improve action when users consult them, while offloading can impair later unaided prospective-memory performance after reminders disappear (reminder study, offloading study).

A logic model makes the intended causal story explicit by connecting program activities to outcomes and identifying who or what should change (CDC logic-model guidance). It should also record contextual factors because external conditions can help or hinder results and change how findings should be interpreted (CDC logic-model guidance). Success is therefore better performance against a documented baseline or feasible alternative, not activity growth alone (UK guidance on defining success, UK service measurement guidance).

The purpose-and-evaluation charter

The core planning artifact should state the audience, validated needs, intended tasks, outcomes, and evidence plan because traceability from implementation work back to needs makes it possible to assess whether each need is being met (UK service guidance on user needs). The charter should estimate the size of the current problem and connect improvement to wider organizational aims or strategies (UK service measurement guidance). It should link activities to intended outcomes through a logic model and record contextual factors that may influence achievement (CDC logic-model guidance).

Objectives should be specific, measurable, achievable, relevant, and time-bound so that progress can be tracked (CDC SMART-objective guidance). The evaluation plan should prioritize a feasible set of questions and short-term timelines instead of attempting to measure everything (CDC SMART-objective guidance). Metrics should be defined before implementation so the team knows whether the system solves its intended problem, then revised as understanding of users improves (UK guidance on defining success).

Raw clippings, transcripts, generated summaries, searches, and contribution counts should be treated as inputs or activity indicators rather than evidence of value unless they improve the defined task or outcome (UK guidance on defining success, APQC measurement guidance). ⚠️ A charter should also specify review points and failure thresholds because performance data is meant to guide decisions about fixing problems and improving the service, not merely to be reported (UK guidance on defining success).

From need to pilot: the operating mechanism

The first step is to observe representative users performing consequential tasks and express their need as a problem rather than a preferred feature (UK service guidance on user needs). The second is to establish a baseline with direct task measures such as completion rate and completion time, which are standard measures for realistic service tests (UK service measurement guidance). The third is to select a mechanism that matches the goal, because reminder checking supports prospective action but cannot establish durable unaided capability (reminder study, offloading study).

The fourth step is to specify the causal chain and its contextual assumptions in a logic model (CDC logic-model guidance). The fifth is to predefine SMART objectives and a feasible set of priority evaluation questions (CDC SMART-objective guidance). The sixth is to pilot with realistic tasks, combining task data with observation or user research because analytics alone cannot show whether users reached the right answer for the right reasons (UK service measurement guidance).

Performance data should then be used to continue, revise, narrow, or stop the intervention, and both metrics and collection practices should evolve as knowledge of user needs improves (UK guidance on defining success). Activity measures can diagnose whether the mechanism is being used, but outcome measures determine whether the system deserves continued effort (UK guidance on defining success, APQC measurement guidance). ⚠️

Personal purposes and guardrails

An individual should begin with a narrow repeated problem whose baseline can be observed, such as refinding a correct source, resuming a project, executing a future intention, or retaining knowledge without the aid (UK service measurement guidance, reminder study, offloading study). A research-oriented system can be judged through realistic retrieval tasks and completion time, while a reminder-oriented system must be judged by completed intentions rather than the number of reminders created (UK service measurement guidance, reminder study).

Reminder use illustrates why intended outcome matters: older adults in one study compensated for poorer internal prospective memory by checking reminders more often, so effectiveness depended on consultation behavior rather than reminder creation alone (reminder study). A controlled design also examined offloaded and non-offloaded intentions under both low and high memory demands, but the corresponding claim is only medium confidence and should not be generalized broadly (reminder study). ⚠️ Another experiment found that immediate offloading benefits could be followed by worse unaided prospective-memory performance than a no-reminder baseline after reminders were removed (offloading study).

If the purpose is reliable external access, dependence on the system may be acceptable, but if the purpose is durable independent competence, later performance without the aid must be a guardrail (offloading study). Personal success criteria should therefore include task completion, time, correctness, and—where learning matters—unaided performance after the external support is withdrawn (UK service measurement guidance, offloading study). Failure includes an aid that improves visible activity while the target task remains unchanged or unaided capability declines where independence is required (UK guidance on defining success, offloading study).

Team and company outcomes

At organizational scale, a second-brain initiative should be managed as an ongoing knowledge-management system rather than a one-time repository launch, because ISO 30401 covers establishment, implementation, maintenance, review, and improvement (ISO 30401). The ISO requirements apply across organizational types and sizes, so the management-cycle principle is not restricted to a particular sector or scale (ISO 30401).

The organizational purpose should connect participation and reuse to an operating result such as performance, cost, or another business outcome rather than treating activity as value in itself (APQC measurement guidance). ⚠️ APQC defines KM measurement as estimating the relationship between adoption or participation and generated business value, but this claim has medium confidence and should be used as guidance rather than a validated universal formula (APQC measurement guidance). ⚠️ The same source warns that measures suited to one KM initiative may be irrelevant to another, making operating-outcome specificity essential (APQC measurement guidance). ⚠️

Teams should combine quantitative performance measures with representative user research because completion rates and time reveal task performance while observation helps explain why a transaction succeeds or fails (UK service measurement guidance). Governance criteria should be reviewed and improved over time because organizational KM is an ongoing managed system and performance evidence should drive decisions (ISO 30401, UK guidance on defining success). Sustained contribution without improvement in the stated operating outcome is not sufficient evidence of success because activity data alone does not establish business value (APQC measurement guidance). ⚠️

Tool-neutral and AI-aware implementation

A defensible implementation begins with an instrumented pilot built around validated needs, predefined metrics, and realistic tasks rather than enterprise-wide ingestion (UK service guidance on user needs, UK guidance on defining success, UK service measurement guidance). Traceability should connect each feature and workflow to a validated need, and the evaluation should record task completion, time, observation, and relevant contextual factors (UK service guidance on user needs, UK service measurement guidance, CDC logic-model guidance).

AI-assisted knowledge systems require a more explicit predeployment contract: the organization’s mission, relevant AI goals, business context, and risk tolerance should be understood and documented (NIST AI RMF). The system’s limits on generalization beyond its development conditions should be documented, and the deployed system should be demonstrated to behave validly and reliably (NIST AI RMF). Failure criteria should include residual risk above tolerance and inability to fail safely when operating beyond knowledge limits (NIST AI RMF).

Evaluation cannot end at launch because NIST calls for regular identification and tracking of existing, unanticipated, and emergent AI risks (NIST AI RMF). An AI second brain should therefore be monitored in the actual use context, with human observation retained alongside dashboards and with metrics revised as needs and risks become clearer (NIST AI RMF, UK guidance on defining success, UK service measurement guidance).

Evidence, scorecards, risks, and stop conditions

The evidence is strongest for user-centered planning, program evaluation, managed KM, prospective-memory effects, and AI risk management rather than for a universal productivity effect of products marketed as second brains (UK service guidance on user needs, CDC logic-model guidance, ISO 30401, reminder study, offloading study, NIST AI RMF). A balanced scorecard should therefore combine direct outcomes, mechanism-use indicators, quality measures, effort or cost, and guardrails, with each measure linked to the defined need and logic model (UK service guidance on user needs, CDC logic-model guidance, UK service measurement guidance).

Task completion and completion time are appropriate direct measures for realistic refinding and knowledge-use tests, but they should be combined with observation or usability research (UK service measurement guidance). Activity counts can help diagnose adoption, yet they do not establish learning, decision, or business value without a demonstrated relationship to downstream results (APQC measurement guidance). ⚠️ Where independent capability matters, testing without the external aid is necessary because offloading can undermine later prospective-memory performance when reminders disappear (offloading study).

Stop or revision conditions should be declared before implementation because predefined success measures reveal whether the intended problem is being solved and performance data should guide improvement decisions (UK guidance on defining success). For AI, stop conditions should include residual risk beyond tolerance, unreliable behavior, unsafe failure outside knowledge limits, or newly emerging risk that cannot be controlled (NIST AI RMF). Remaining uncertainty concerns causal attribution in knowledge work, long-run maintenance burden, effects across expertise levels, and how long an observation period must be to distinguish durable benefit from novelty, because the cited guidance establishes evaluation design principles rather than answers to those empirical questions (CDC logic-model guidance, UK guidance on defining success).

Tensions: A system optimized for dependable external access can rationally substitute reminders for internal prospective memory, while a system intended to build durable unaided competence must treat later dependence as a failure mode (reminder study, offloading study). Usage and contribution metrics are easy mechanism indicators, but they do not establish performance, cost savings, learning, or business value without outcome evidence (APQC measurement guidance). ⚠️ Broad measurement promises completeness, yet CDC guidance recommends a feasible set of priority questions and short-term timelines rather than attempting to evaluate everything (CDC SMART-objective guidance). Standardized management supports maintenance, review, and improvement, while the evidence here does not establish one generic metric set for every knowledge-management purpose (ISO 30401, APQC measurement guidance). ⚠️

Unanswered questions: None recorded.

2.2 Knowledge and content model

The model as an explicit representation contract

A second-brain content model is a contract for representing resources, annotations, claims, people, activities, and their relationships rather than an assertion that all knowledge can be reduced to records (W3C PROV-O, Web Annotation). Its first discipline is separation: PROV-O distinguishes Entity, Activity, and Agent, while Web Annotation represents an annotation as an object connecting a body to at least one target (W3C PROV-O, Web Annotation). This prevents a source artifact, a statement about it, the process that transformed it, and the responsible person or system from collapsing into one undifferentiated record (W3C PROV-O, Web Annotation).

Provenance relations should be explicit because derivation describes the transformation, update, or construction of one entity from another, whereas attribution assigns responsibility for an entity to an agent (W3C PROV-O). Lifecycle state is separate again: PROV-O can represent invalidation as the start of an entity’s destruction, cessation, or expiry without erasing its history (W3C PROV-O). Authority should likewise not be inferred from proximity because metadata copied into an annotation about an external body or target is only a client hint and is not authoritative for that external resource (Web Annotation).

The model should remain purpose-driven and incremental because FAIR provides implementation-independent principles rather than mandating a technology, standard, or formal specification (FAIR principles). Dublin Core, PROV-O, Web Annotation, SHACL, SKOS, DataCite, and records standards therefore function as complementary vocabularies and controls rather than as one universal ontology (Dublin Core, W3C PROV-O, Web Annotation, SHACL, SKOS, DataCite schema, ISO 15489-1).

Objects, fields, and relationships

At minimum, the model needs identifiable resources, agents, activities, annotations, and concepts because provenance, interpretation, and vocabulary depend on those distinct structures (W3C PROV-O, Web Annotation, SKOS). A resource record can reuse Dublin Core’s broad set of properties, classes, datatypes, and vocabulary schemes for descriptive metadata (Dublin Core). These terms are not tied to RDF storage and can be reused in JSON, XML, UML, or relational models (Dublin Core).

Each reusable object should have a persistent identity, rich metadata, and searchable registration or indexing under the FAIR findability principles (FAIR principles). Citation-oriented objects can use DataCite’s core metadata properties for consistent identification, citation, and retrieval; the DataCite documentation reports schema version 4.7 as its latest minor version (DataCite schema). Reusability also requires detailed provenance, clear usage licensing, and alignment with relevant domain standards (FAIR principles).

Annotations should remain first-class objects with at least one target, and their body or target may identify a particular segment or state rather than only an entire resource (Web Annotation). Their intent should be recorded explicitly as a motivation so a quotation, correction, classification, or other interpretive act is not stripped of purpose (Web Annotation).

Core provenance relationships include derivation between generated and used entities and attribution between an entity and its responsible agent (W3C PROV-O). Dublin Core adds relations for custody and ownership changes that affect authenticity, integrity, or interpretation, as well as an explicit relation to a resource superseded by the described resource (Dublin Core). Rights metadata should distinguish information about rights from the person or organization that owns or manages those rights (Dublin Core).

Concepts need their own vocabulary layer because SKOS distinguishes preferred, alternative, and hidden lexical labels and supplies direct broader and narrower links (SKOS). Those semantic links allow concepts to form a hierarchy without forcing every knowledge artifact into a single folder tree (SKOS).

From user question to governed lifecycle

Modeling should begin with what a user or agent must be able to find, distinguish, trace, compare, or decide, then select only the structures necessary to answer those questions (FAIR principles, DataCite schema). Capture should preserve a source as an entity, represent interpretation as a separate annotation or derived entity, and record the activity and agent responsible for the transformation (W3C PROV-O, Web Annotation). This yields a traversable path from a claim or synthesis back to its exact target segment and responsible transformation (W3C PROV-O, Web Annotation).

Identity and vocabulary management should use stable identifiers and explicit label mappings because FAIR requires globally unique persistent identifiers and SKOS separates preferred, alternative, and hidden labels (FAIR principles, SKOS). Suspected aliases should not be silently merged when identity is uncertain because the standards support identifiers and multiple labels without requiring every label to denote the same entity (FAIR principles, SKOS).

Validation must check the model rather than infer correctness from successful ingestion: SHACL shapes can express value, node-kind, datatype, pattern, and cardinality constraints (SHACL). A focus node conforms only when validation returns no results and no failure, while an ill-formed shapes graph makes the validation outcome undefined (SHACL). The validation rules therefore require their own integrity checks before their reports can be trusted (SHACL).

Versioning should preserve meaningful change relationships: DataCite recommends a new identifier for major content changes linked to the previous version, while minor changes may retain the identifier with updated version metadata (DataCite versioning). The distinction between major and minor change is a stewardship decision rather than a universal rule (DataCite versioning). Supersession should be represented as a relation between resources instead of being inferred from timestamps alone (Dublin Core).

Disposition is part of the same lifecycle because records schedules specify whether series are temporary or permanent, how long they are retained, and what happens when they are no longer needed for current business (US National Archives). Invalidation and disposition should preserve appropriate history rather than simply deleting every trace of the prior object (W3C PROV-O, US National Archives).

A minimal personal content model

For an individual, a minimal model can begin with stable identity, basic descriptive metadata, source links, and explicit annotation relationships because those structures enable findability, interpretation, and provenance without requiring a universal ontology (FAIR principles, Dublin Core, Web Annotation). A quotation or paraphrase should not overwrite its source: it should be modeled as a body directed at the whole source or an exact segment, with its motivation recorded (Web Annotation). A derived note should link back to the used entity and record the responsible agent or activity so later readers can distinguish authorship from source authority (W3C PROV-O).

Personal concepts can use a preferred label plus alternative or hidden labels, adding broader or narrower relations only when retrieval needs justify them (SKOS). Major revisions can receive new identifiers linked to prior versions, while minor revisions can retain identity and update version metadata according to a stated stewardship policy (DataCite versioning). Rights ownership should remain distinct from descriptive rights information, especially when the note and its source have different creators or rights holders (Dublin Core).

Private material still needs content boundaries because accessibility under FAIR does not require unrestricted access and may include authentication and authorization (FAIR principles). Retention should be intentional rather than indefinite because records schedules explicitly distinguish temporary from permanent material and define disposition after current business need ends (US National Archives). Metadata can remain available after data is removed under FAIR, but whether that is appropriate for a sensitive personal object requires a separate privacy decision because persistence is a principle, not an unconditional command (FAIR principles).

Shared knowledge, authority, and governance

Team and company systems need explicit roles, policies, responsibilities, controls, and lifecycle processes because ISO 15489-1 includes records, records metadata, policies, assigned responsibilities, monitoring, and training within records management (ISO 15489-1). Those principles apply across record structures, forms, business environments, and technological environments over time (ISO 15489-1). A shared model should therefore distinguish creator, contributor, responsible agent, rights holder, custodian, and current steward rather than compressing them into one “owner” field (W3C PROV-O, Dublin Core, ISO 15489-1).

Approval and authority should remain separate from truth and provenance because attribution only identifies responsibility, and annotation metadata about external resources is explicitly non-authoritative (W3C PROV-O, Web Annotation). Competing interpretations can be modeled as separate annotations directed at the same target, each with its own motivation and provenance, instead of overwriting disagreement with one statement (Web Annotation, W3C PROV-O). Superseded material can remain linked through explicit relations and invalidation events, preserving the sequence of organizational judgment (Dublin Core, W3C PROV-O).

Shared vocabularies should maintain preferred, alternative, and hidden labels plus broader and narrower concept relationships so local language can be mapped without forcing every artifact into one physical hierarchy (SKOS). Access control can coexist with findability because FAIR allows authentication and authorization in standardized retrieval protocols (FAIR principles). Rights metadata and the agent managing rights should remain separate, allowing governance decisions to be attached without confusing them with descriptive content (Dublin Core).

Records governance must include disposition because schedules state whether record series are temporary or permanent and how long to retain them (US National Archives). The content model should represent that decision and its lifecycle event instead of assuming that all organizational knowledge should be preserved indefinitely (US National Archives, W3C PROV-O).

Standards-based implementation patterns

A practical architecture can combine a canonical content store with typed metadata, vocabulary services, provenance relations, validation, and retrieval views because the cited standards cover those functions independently (Dublin Core, SKOS, W3C PROV-O, SHACL, FAIR principles). Storage technology can vary because Dublin Core terms work in RDF and non-RDF environments including JSON, XML, UML, and relational databases, while FAIR does not prescribe a specific implementation (Dublin Core, FAIR principles).

Dublin Core supplies reusable descriptive metadata and relations such as provenance, rights-holder, and supersession (Dublin Core). PROV-O supplies Entity, Activity, Agent, derivation, attribution, and invalidation structures (W3C PROV-O). Web Annotation supplies body, target, exact-segment, state, and motivation patterns while warning that copied external metadata is not authoritative (Web Annotation). SKOS supplies concept labels and direct broader or narrower links (SKOS). DataCite supplies core identification, citation, retrieval, and version-linking patterns (DataCite schema, DataCite versioning). SHACL supplies machine-readable graph constraints and validation results, subject to the validity of the shapes graph itself (SHACL).

FAIR provides the cross-cutting goals: persistent identity and rich indexed metadata for findability, controlled standardized retrieval for accessibility, and provenance, licensing, and domain standards for reuse (FAIR principles). It also allows metadata to remain accessible after the underlying data disappears, a useful provenance pattern that must still be reconciled with privacy and retention requirements (FAIR principles, US National Archives).

Evidence, evaluation, risks, and evolving boundaries

The evidence base is standards-heavy and strongly supports interoperable representation patterns, but FAIR explicitly says its principles are not themselves a technology, standard, or specification (FAIR principles). The standards establish ways to describe resources, provenance, annotations, concepts, constraints, versions, and retention; they do not establish that the richest possible schema improves every second-brain outcome (Dublin Core, W3C PROV-O, Web Annotation, SKOS, SHACL, DataCite versioning, US National Archives).

Evaluation should therefore use realistic tasks such as correct retrieval, provenance reconstruction, authority discrimination, version tracing, and retention execution rather than field completion alone (FAIR principles, W3C PROV-O, Dublin Core, US National Archives). Validation metrics can count SHACL failures, but conformance is meaningful only when the shapes graph is itself well formed (SHACL). Version-quality measures can check whether major changes receive new linked identifiers and whether stewardship rules distinguish major from minor revisions consistently (DataCite versioning).

Risks arise when structure is mistaken for truth: attribution establishes responsibility but not correctness, copied annotation metadata is non-authoritative, and a checksum or identifier cannot by itself establish authenticity, lawfulness, or epistemic validity (W3C PROV-O, Web Annotation, FAIR principles). Rich identity and relationship metadata can also persist after content deletion under FAIR, creating a tension with disposition and sensitive-data boundaries (FAIR principles, US National Archives). Boundaries should evolve through explicit vocabulary, validation, versioning, and disposition decisions rather than uncontrolled property growth (SKOS, SHACL, DataCite versioning, US National Archives).

Tensions: Richer metadata improves findability, provenance, validation, and reuse, but the standards do not prove that maximum schema complexity improves every use case (FAIR principles, SHACL). Stable identifiers and preferred labels reduce ambiguity, while alternative and hidden labels and steward-defined version boundaries show that identity and change retain legitimate interpretive flexibility (FAIR principles, SKOS, DataCite versioning). Keeping metadata accessible after content deletion supports provenance and discovery, yet records schedules require explicit disposition and do not imply that every trace should remain forever (FAIR principles, US National Archives). Canonical supersession supports operational clarity, while separate annotations and preserved invalidation history allow dissent and obsolete rationales to remain auditable (Dublin Core, Web Annotation, W3C PROV-O). Exact source retention improves traceability, but authentication, authorization, rights management, and disposition can legitimately restrict access or require removal (FAIR principles, Dublin Core, US National Archives).

Unanswered questions: None recorded.

2.3 Platform architecture, interoperability, and portability

Architecture as replaceable capabilities and tested exit paths

A durable second brain should be designed as a set of replaceable capabilities rather than as an indivisible application because cloud portability includes both workload portability and data portability (NIST cloud standards roadmap). Portability is broader than downloading content: the system’s executable workload, data, metadata, relationships, interfaces, and recovery procedures may require distinct mechanisms (NIST cloud standards roadmap). The claim that a standards-based cloud exit specifically needs separate mechanisms for data and system portability is medium confidence, so it should guide testing rather than be treated as a universal architecture law (NIST cloud standards roadmap). ⚠️

Interoperability also cannot be reduced to a “standards-based” label because cloud-specific portability standards coexist with data and metadata standards created before cloud computing (NIST cloud standards roadmap). The Library of Congress advises evaluating a format by disclosure, adoption, transparency, self-documentation, external dependencies, patents, and technical protection mechanisms (Library of Congress format guidance). Complete documentation and independent validation matter more for sustainability than approval by a recognized standards body alone (Library of Congress format guidance).

Resilience is a further, separate property because contingency planning coordinates plans, procedures, and technical measures to recover systems, operations, and data after disruption (NIST contingency planning). An export is not yet evidence of resilience until its backup is tested and reviewed in a recovery exercise (NIST backup guidance).

The canonical preservation set

The preservation set should retain the content needed by users plus enough representation, reference, context, fixity, and provenance information to interpret it over time (Library of Congress format guidance). Long-term preservation must anticipate changing technologies, media, data formats, and the knowledge base of the intended community (OAIS). In OAIS, “open” describes standards development in open forums and does not imply unrestricted archive access (OAIS).

Format selection should account for genre-specific characteristics expected by future users rather than applying one generic score to every content type (Library of Congress format guidance). Widely adopted formats are less likely to become obsolete quickly and are more likely to attract migration or emulation tools (Library of Congress format guidance). Human-readable or directly analyzable representations are generally easier to inspect, migrate, and recover with basic tools (Library of Congress format guidance).

A transfer package can use BagIt to bundle arbitrary digital payloads with descriptive tags without requiring the packaging layer to understand the payload’s internal semantics (BagIt RFC). Its payload manifest lists every payload file with a checksum, and a valid bag requires successful verification of every checksum in payload and tag manifests (BagIt RFC). Those checksums detect integrity failures but do not make the package secure against active attacks or prove that the export is semantically complete (BagIt RFC).

Architecture records should therefore distinguish bit-level fixity from semantic completeness: a package can pass checksum verification while still omitting a relationship, permission, version, or externally referenced object (BagIt RFC, Library of Congress format guidance).

The operating flow: store, synchronize, back up, and restore

A robust operating flow commits canonical information in a documented format, records the preservation metadata needed for future interpretation, packages or snapshots it, verifies fixity, and periodically restores it in a recovery exercise (Library of Congress format guidance, BagIt RFC, NIST backup guidance). Backup operations should be integrated with change management rather than treated as an unrelated periodic task (NIST backup guidance). Effective backup management requires regular backup creation, testing, and review during recovery exercises (NIST backup guidance).

Remote authoring can use WebDAV, which standardizes operations for resource properties, collections, locking, and namespace moves or copies (WebDAV RFC). WebDAV locking is intended to reduce lost updates during concurrent authoring, but compliant resources are not required to support locking (WebDAV RFC). A synchronization design must therefore document its actual concurrency guarantees rather than infer them from protocol use alone (WebDAV RFC).

Contingency plans may restore systems with alternate equipment or locations and may temporarily run some business processes through manual alternatives (NIST contingency planning). Recovery evidence should demonstrate that critical knowledge tasks can continue or resume through these declared mechanisms rather than merely showing that stored bytes exist (NIST contingency planning, NIST backup guidance).

Personal architecture and recovery discipline

For an individual, human-readable canonical text is a strong portability signal because transparent representations are open to direct analysis with basic tools, including a text-only editor (Library of Congress format guidance). CommonMark provides a versioned specification for interoperable Markdown parsing, and every character sequence remains a valid CommonMark document (CommonMark). CommonMark does not mandate a byte encoding, so a portable personal profile should declare one, such as UTF-8, rather than assuming character encoding will be inferred correctly (CommonMark).

An embedded SQLite store is another portable option because SQLite states that its database files are bit-for-bit identical across common 32-bit, 64-bit, big-endian, and little-endian architectures (SQLite long-term support). SQLite explicitly presents the portability of both its code and file format as part of its long-term viability rationale (SQLite long-term support). A database file still requires backup testing and recovery exercises, because stable representation does not by itself demonstrate recoverability (SQLite long-term support, NIST backup guidance).

Structured relationships can be stored in JSON-LD because every JSON-LD document is valid JSON and the format is intended for interoperable web services and linked-data storage in JSON-based engines (JSON-LD 1.1). JSON-LD 1.1 generally preserves compatibility with documents written for JSON-LD 1.0, except where the specification notes otherwise (JSON-LD 1.1).

A personal exit test should package representative content, verify its manifests, restore it with independent tools, and confirm that the restored material remains interpretable to its intended user (BagIt RFC, OAIS). An implementation inextricably bound to one device or blocking authorized backup and disaster recovery is unsuitable for long-term preservation (Library of Congress format guidance).

Team and company architecture

Teams must plan for both data and workload portability because organizational exit may require more than bulk record export (NIST cloud standards roadmap). Their contingency strategy should coordinate plans, procedures, and technical measures across information systems, operations, and data rather than leave recovery to a storage operator alone (NIST contingency planning). Alternate equipment, alternate locations, and limited manual operation are legitimate resilience mechanisms for disrupted processes (NIST contingency planning).

Procurement and architecture review should examine format disclosure, adoption, transparency, self-documentation, external dependencies, patents, and technical protection mechanisms (Library of Congress format guidance). A vendor’s standards claim is insufficient when complete documentation, independent validation tools, or workable migration paths are absent (Library of Congress format guidance). Long-term plans should also account for changes in technology, media, formats, and the designated user community rather than assume today’s environment will persist (OAIS).

Backups should be tied to change management, created regularly, tested, and reviewed during recovery exercises (NIST backup guidance). Transfer packages can use BagIt manifests and checksums to measure whether all packaged files arrived intact, but active-attack protection and semantic reconciliation need additional controls (BagIt RFC). A migration rehearsal should therefore validate both file integrity and the usability of restored content, because fixity covers bits while preservation also requires representation, reference, context, and provenance (BagIt RFC, Library of Congress format guidance).

Open archive architecture does not mean unrestricted access because OAIS explicitly separates open standards development from access policy (OAIS). Organizations can therefore combine controlled access with preservation and portability, provided authorized recovery and migration remain possible (OAIS, Library of Congress format guidance).

Implementation patterns and technology choices

A file-centered pattern can use CommonMark for narrative content, an explicitly declared encoding, JSON-LD for structured relationships, and BagIt for transfer manifests and checksum verification (CommonMark, JSON-LD 1.1, BagIt RFC). This pattern emphasizes transparency because CommonMark accepts any character sequence and transparent formats are directly analyzable with basic tools (CommonMark, Library of Congress format guidance).

A database-centered pattern can use SQLite when a stable cross-platform file representation and low-dependency local storage are important (SQLite long-term support). SQLite’s portable file format is a preservation advantage, but the database still needs documented export and tested recovery because all backups must be exercised rather than assumed valid (SQLite long-term support, NIST backup guidance).

A linked-data pattern can use JSON-LD to add graph semantics while remaining compatible with ordinary JSON tooling and interoperable web services (JSON-LD 1.1). A remote-authoring pattern can use WebDAV for properties, collections, locking, moves, and copies, but implementations must verify whether locking is actually supported (WebDAV RFC).

A preservation pattern can package arbitrary payloads with BagIt and retain representation, reference, context, fixity, and provenance metadata for long-term interpretation (BagIt RFC, Library of Congress format guidance). It should reject device-bound or backup-blocking designs because those arrangements are unsuitable for authorized long-term preservation (Library of Congress format guidance).

A managed-cloud or hybrid pattern must retain a tested exit for both workload and data because cloud portability covers both categories (NIST cloud standards roadmap). The architecture choice should be evaluated through exported content, independent restoration, and contingency performance rather than through a local-versus-cloud label alone (NIST backup guidance, NIST contingency planning).

Evidence, metrics, risks, and review triggers

The evidence here consists mainly of mature standards and institutional preservation, backup, and contingency guidance rather than comparative trials of second-brain platforms (NIST cloud standards roadmap, Library of Congress format guidance, NIST backup guidance, OAIS). Architecture should therefore be evaluated through demonstrated export, checksum verification, restore, migration, and task continuity rather than inferred product quality (BagIt RFC, NIST backup guidance, NIST contingency planning).

Useful metrics include the proportion of expected payload files present, manifest-checksum success, restore success and time, independent-tool readability, and recovery of representation, reference, context, and provenance information (BagIt RFC, Library of Congress format guidance, NIST backup guidance). Workload and data should be tested separately where cloud portability is in scope (NIST cloud standards roadmap). WebDAV deployments should measure lost updates and actual lock support because locking is designed to reduce concurrency loss but is optional (WebDAV RFC).

Checksums cannot detect a logically incomplete export and do not secure a package against active attacks (BagIt RFC). A successful restore into the original environment does not by itself demonstrate portability because portability encompasses movement of both workload and data to another environment (NIST cloud standards roadmap). Encryption or technical protection that inextricably binds content to a device or blocks authorized backup and disaster recovery undermines long-term preservation (Library of Congress format guidance).

Architecture should be reviewed when technologies, formats, media, or the intended community changes, because long-term preservation explicitly anticipates those shifts (OAIS). Backup design should also be revisited during system change because NIST recommends integrating backups with change management (NIST backup guidance).

Tensions: Transparent plain-text formats support direct inspection and tool diversity, while SQLite offers a stable structured database representation; neither removes the need for independent backup and recovery tests (Library of Congress format guidance, CommonMark, SQLite long-term support, NIST backup guidance). Managed cloud services can support workload and data portability only when their exit mechanisms are documented and tested, so service convenience does not eliminate provider dependency (NIST cloud standards roadmap). Encryption protects access, yet device-bound or backup-blocking protection can prevent authorized preservation and recovery (Library of Congress format guidance). Remote synchronization supports collaborative authoring, but optional locking means protocol compliance alone cannot guarantee protection from concurrent lost updates (WebDAV RFC). Preserving every derivative can speed exact recovery, while packaging only canonical payloads reduces dependency; BagIt verifies the files included but cannot determine whether the selected package was semantically complete (BagIt RFC).

Unanswered questions: None recorded.

2.4 AI context engineering and machine-usable memory

Memory as a controlled projection, not a second truth store

An AI memory layer should be treated as a controlled projection of a canonical knowledge repository because retrieval-augmented generation explicitly combines a model’s parametric memory with non-parametric external memory (RAG paper). The original RAG study reported state-of-the-art performance on three open-domain question-answering tasks, but it also identified provenance and world-knowledge updating as open problems (RAG paper). External retrieval therefore adds useful evidence access without making the model or retrieved store automatically authoritative (RAG paper).

More context is not automatically better because long-context model performance can change substantially when the same relevant information appears at different positions (Lost in the Middle). Relevant material placed in the middle is often used less effectively than material at the beginning or end, and a larger context window does not guarantee robust use of every supplied item (Lost in the Middle). The design target should therefore be sufficient, relevant, current, authorized, and attributable context rather than maximum token volume (Lost in the Middle, RAG paper).

Hierarchical memory can move information between a fast active context and slower external tiers, but the MemGPT evidence is a medium-confidence prototype rather than a general proof of durable agent memory (MemGPT). ⚠️ MemGPT manages multiple memory tiers to extend effective context within a bounded model window and was evaluated in document analysis and multi-session chat (MemGPT). ⚠️ These tiers are functional computer-system categories and should not be mistaken for evidence that an agent remembers as a person does (MemGPT). ⚠️

Machine-usable objects and provenance

Machine-usable memory should retain source segments, assertions, responsible agents, transformation history, timestamps, scope, and status because RAG does not by itself solve provenance or knowledge updating (RAG paper). Retrieval artifacts should also record queries, candidates, selected context, and citations so a generated answer can be traced to the non-parametric evidence that influenced it (RAG paper). Generated summaries should remain derived artifacts rather than silently replacing their sources because summarization is inherently lossy in the cited compaction study (compaction study). ⚠️

Long-term conversational memory needs separate representations and tests for information extraction, multi-session reasoning, temporal reasoning, knowledge updates, and abstention (LongMemEval). LongMemEval uses 500 curated questions embedded in scalable user-assistant histories and reported a 30 percent accuracy drop for commercial assistants and long-context models on sustained-interaction memory (LongMemEval). A machine memory record should consequently preserve time, update status, and links to replaced or contradictory assertions rather than store only an unqualified fact string (LongMemEval).

Tool and agent interfaces add further artifacts. MCP separates messaging, lifecycle, authorization, server features, client features, and utilities into modular components, requires JSON-RPC 2.0 messages, and uses JSON Schema throughout protocol validation (MCP base protocol). MCP tools expose declared schemas for operations such as database queries, API calls, and computations (MCP tools). A2A represents stateful tasks with unique identifiers and defined lifecycles, while distinguishing conversational messages from generated artifacts composed of typed parts (A2A specification). These structures support machine-readable task state and handoff without requiring free-form transcript interpretation alone (MCP base protocol, A2A specification).

Retrieval, active context, compaction, and forgetting

The operational loop begins by identifying the task and its authorized scope, retrieving candidate external evidence, selecting a bounded context, generating or acting, and preserving citations back to the supporting material because RAG joins model generation to non-parametric memory without eliminating provenance requirements (RAG paper). Position should be treated as part of context engineering because identical relevant information can produce different results depending on where it appears in a long input (Lost in the Middle). Context selection should therefore be evaluated for both retrieval relevance and effective model use rather than assuming all inserted evidence receives equal attention (Lost in the Middle).

Long-term evaluation should isolate extraction, cross-session reasoning, temporal reasoning, updates, and abstention because these are distinct memory abilities in LongMemEval (LongMemEval). The benchmark’s reported accuracy drop on sustained interactions shows that simply retaining a long transcript does not establish reliable memory behavior (LongMemEval).

Compaction trades token cost for fidelity because summarization is inherently lossy, can stall inference for tens of seconds in the cited study, and can retain different amounts of information across runs (compaction study). ⚠️ A compacted state should therefore retain links to uncompressed history and preserve decisions, unresolved obligations, identifiers, dates, citations, and uncertainty where the task depends on them, although the exact optimal compaction policy remains uncertain (compaction study, LongMemEval). ⚠️

Forgetting and correction should be designed as explicit state changes because people have rights to access stored personal data, rectify inaccurate or incomplete data, and request erasure or restriction where applicable (ICO individual-rights guidance). Knowledge-update evaluation should verify that corrected information supersedes stale information and that the assistant abstains when memory is insufficient (LongMemEval).

Personal memory controls and agency

Individuals should be able to inspect and receive a copy of stored personal data because access and receipt of a copy are recognized data rights (ICO individual-rights guidance). They should also be able to correct inaccurate or incomplete memories and exercise erasure or restriction rights where applicable (ICO individual-rights guidance). Data portability should support obtaining and reusing personal data across services rather than trapping personalization in one provider’s latent state (ICO individual-rights guidance).

A personal memory interface should expose what was stored, its source, its time and scope, and its correction history because RAG leaves provenance and updating unresolved and LongMemEval treats temporal reasoning and knowledge updates as separate capabilities (RAG paper, LongMemEval). A correction should create a traceable replacement that is favored over the superseded assertion rather than merely adding contradiction, because update accuracy must be evaluated explicitly (LongMemEval).

Temporary use and memory pause are important design controls when a user does not want an interaction promoted into durable memory, although the cited rights guidance establishes access, correction, erasure, restriction, and portability rather than a universal interface design (ICO individual-rights guidance). The safest conclusion is that controls must make the legally and operationally supported actions effective and inspectable, while the exact presentation remains context-dependent (ICO individual-rights guidance, NIST AI RMF).

Human oversight should be defined, assessed, and documented for AI systems, especially when memory can influence consequential actions or tool use (NIST AI RMF). MCP specifically recommends preserving a human ability to deny tool invocations, and clients must treat tool annotations as untrusted unless they come from trusted servers (MCP tools).

Team and enterprise memory

At organizational scale, the targeted AI application scope should be documented from system capability, established context, and system categorization (NIST AI RMF). Human oversight processes should be defined, assessed, and documented, and risk mapping should include third-party software and data components (NIST AI RMF). These requirements make enterprise memory an access-control and accountability system as well as a retrieval feature (NIST AI RMF).

Agent and tool protocols improve interoperability but do not remove governance. MCP’s modular layers include authorization, its messages use JSON-RPC 2.0, its structures use JSON Schema, and its tools may reach databases, APIs, or computations (MCP base protocol, MCP tools). Tool annotations remain untrusted unless the server is trusted, and consequential invocations should preserve a human denial path (MCP tools).

A2A supports interoperability among agents built with different frameworks, languages, or vendors and can exchange information without exposing each agent’s internal state, memory, or tools (A2A specification). It represents work as a stateful task with a unique ID and defined lifecycle and treats generated documents, images, or structured data as artifacts distinct from conversational messages (A2A specification). Enterprise handoffs can therefore exchange task state and artifacts without sharing unrestricted internal memory, provided the organization still applies its own authorization and oversight (A2A specification, NIST AI RMF).

Personal-data obligations remain relevant in shared memory because people may have rights of access, rectification, erasure, restriction, and portability (ICO individual-rights guidance). Derived summaries, indexes, and agent artifacts should therefore be included in deletion and correction design when they contain the affected personal data, although the exact propagation mechanism is not resolved by the cited sources (ICO individual-rights guidance, compaction study). ⚠️

Implementation patterns and open protocols

A representative implementation keeps canonical evidence outside the model and builds retrieval over it, combining parametric generation with selected non-parametric memory (RAG paper). It should test both relevance and placement because long-context performance varies with the location of relevant information and does not improve reliably merely by enlarging the window (Lost in the Middle).

Hierarchical memory can maintain a small active context and move less immediate information into external tiers, as demonstrated by the MemGPT prototype (MemGPT). ⚠️ Because MemGPT was evaluated only in document analysis and multi-session chat, this architecture should be treated as a prototype pattern rather than proof of durable enterprise memory (MemGPT). ⚠️ Compaction can reduce active context, but the cited 2026 work reports lossiness, latency, and run-to-run variability, so summaries require provenance and regression testing (compaction study). ⚠️

MCP can expose application-controlled capabilities through modular client-server messaging, JSON-RPC 2.0, JSON Schema validation, and declared tool contracts (MCP base protocol, MCP tools). Its security posture requires untrusted tool annotations to remain untrusted and preserves a recommended human denial capability (MCP tools).

A2A can serve agent-to-agent handoff by exchanging messages, stateful task identifiers, lifecycles, and typed artifacts across framework and vendor boundaries without disclosing internal memory (A2A specification). Protocol compatibility still requires scope documentation, third-party risk mapping, and human oversight because those governance duties apply to the complete AI system (NIST AI RMF).

Evidence, evaluation, threats, and unresolved design choices

The evidence supports constituent mechanisms rather than mature multi-year memory deployments: RAG demonstrates parametric plus non-parametric generation, Lost in the Middle documents position effects, LongMemEval benchmarks sustained-interaction abilities, MemGPT demonstrates a hierarchical prototype, and recent compaction work reports lossy and variable summarization (RAG paper, Lost in the Middle, LongMemEval, MemGPT, compaction study). ⚠️ The weak marker applies because the MemGPT and compaction claims are medium confidence even though the RAG, long-context, and LongMemEval claims are solid (MemGPT, compaction study). ⚠️

Evaluation should separately measure retrieval, answer correctness, provenance, temporal reasoning, updates, abstention, and context-position robustness because the studies identify these as distinct failure surfaces (RAG paper, Lost in the Middle, LongMemEval). Compaction tests should measure information loss, latency, and run-to-run variation (compaction study). ⚠️ User-control tests should verify access, copy, rectification, erasure, restriction, and portability actions where applicable (ICO individual-rights guidance).

Threat testing should include untrusted tool annotations, third-party software and data, and consequential tool use without adequate human oversight because the cited MCP and NIST guidance identifies those control points (MCP tools, NIST AI RMF). Interoperability tests should verify that A2A task IDs, lifecycle state, messages, and artifacts move between heterogeneous agents without requiring disclosure of internal memory (A2A specification).

Tensions: Automatic memory writing can improve continuity, but RAG leaves provenance and updating unresolved and personal-data rights require correction, erasure, restriction, and portability where applicable (RAG paper, ICO individual-rights guidance). Long contexts preserve more history, yet models do not use all positions equally; retrieval and compaction reduce the active window, but summarization is lossy and variable (Lost in the Middle, compaction study). ⚠️ Forgetting supports rectification and erasure, while sustained-interaction systems also need history for temporal reasoning and knowledge updates (ICO individual-rights guidance, LongMemEval). Personalization can improve continuity, but its memories must remain accessible, correctable, erasable, restrictable, and portable where those rights apply (ICO individual-rights guidance). Open tool and agent protocols improve interoperability, yet untrusted annotations, third-party components, and cross-system actions expand the governance surface (MCP tools, A2A specification, NIST AI RMF).

Unanswered questions: None recorded.

3. Knowledge lifecycle

The iterative flow by which potentially useful knowledge is selected, captured, structured, validated, retrieved, applied, maintained, and retired.

The knowledge lifecycle is an iterative control loop rather than a one-way pipeline: selection affects later retrieval, retrieval failures expose missing or poorly organized material, action creates new evidence, and review can return an artifact for correction, revalidation, or disposal. Knowledge-audit study DCC Curation Lifecycle Model ⚠️ Its practical stages are purpose-bounded capture, task-contingent organization, risk-tiered validation, context-sensitive retrieval and sensemaking, traceable synthesis and action, and continuing stewardship. Keeping-found-things-found research NIST information-quality standards DCC Curation Lifecycle Model ⚠️ The lifecycle succeeds when knowledge remains usable for a defined task and can change understanding, decisions, or action—not when a system merely accumulates more notes, links, or graph edges. Keeping-found-things-found research ICAP framework ⚠️

Selection and capture begin with a real question, decision, process, obligation, or risk because keeping too little can make needed information unavailable later, while keeping too much creates attention and maintenance costs. Keeping-found-things-found research Information overload has been associated with poorer decisions, lower productivity, and cognitive pressure, so cheaper capture does not remove the need for prioritization and expiry. Information-overload review Durable captures should preserve their source and exact target segment where feasible, while organization should add only the stable identifiers, contextual metadata, labels, links, facets, or navigable containers that recurring retrieval tasks justify. W3C Web Annotation SKOS A hybrid, progressive structure is therefore more defensible than either complete preclassification or structure-free search, because empirical findings vary across folders, tags, facets, navigation, and search contexts. File-management review Email-organization study ⚠️

Validation should treat fitness for a specified use and time as distinct from a universal truth stamp, keeping accuracy, evidentiary certainty, authority, relevance, freshness, and integrity as separate dimensions. NIST information-quality standards Cochrane Handbook Provenance and signatures can establish association, change history, and tamper evidence without proving that an assertion is true, while explicit correction, supersession, and current-status records keep later users from mistaking an obsolete version for governing knowledge. C2PA specification Crossmark Retrieval then has to support several different behaviors: known-item re-finding, evolving exploratory search, intentional resurfacing, collaborative sensemaking, expertise location, and machine-readable evidence assembly for agents. Keeping-found-things-found study Berrypicking model SearchTogether TREC RAG 2025 Because relevance changes with consumer, task, time, and consequence, results should retain status, provenance, access context, and enough session history to explain why an item appeared and how it informed the emerging interpretation. Berrypicking model TREC RAG 2025 ⚠️

The value-creation boundary lies beyond retrieval, where evidence is transformed into an explanatory frame, a warranted synthesis, a novel and useful proposal, a committed choice, or an observable action. ICAP framework Oslo Manual Constructive learning generates inferences or relationships beyond supplied material, while interactive work can co-construct knowledge, so fluent compression or copied summaries are not sufficient evidence of understanding. ICAP framework Synthesis and decision records should retain claims, exact evidence, uncertainty, alternatives, trade-offs, dissent, accountable authority, and expected outcomes, while action records connect choices to owners, cues, resources, verification criteria, and observed results. W3C PROV Data Model Structured decision making ⚠️ Outcomes then feed back into the corpus as observations, corrections, lessons, or changed assumptions, closing a traceable loop from question and evidence through interpretation, decision, action, and revision. NASA Systems Engineering Handbook W3C PROV Data Model ⚠️

Lifecycle stewardship keeps that loop trustworthy by distinguishing current, review-due, stale, superseded, revoked, archived, retained-under-hold, and deleted states rather than treating maintenance as cosmetic cleanup. RFC 9111 Digital Preservation Handbook Review must test current fitness for use, repair broken context, preserve variant provenance when consolidating, route historical evidence to archives, honor retention and privacy obligations, and verify deletion across primary and derived stores when disposal is authorized. Digital Preservation Handbook ICO storage-limitation guidance NIST media-sanitization guidance The same lifecycle logic applies at personal, team, enterprise, and agentic scales, but roles, assurance thresholds, access boundaries, automation, evidence requirements, and operating costs change materially with consequence and deployment scope. NIST information-quality standards NIST Generative AI Profile ⚠️ The deployment profiles that follow therefore specialize this common lifecycle into different ownership, governance, technology, and measurement arrangements rather than replacing it with separate conceptual models. DCC Curation Lifecycle Model NIST information-quality standards ⚠️

3.1 Identify, select, prioritize, and capture

Capture is a selection problem, not a volume target

Capture should be treated as a purpose-constrained decision under uncertainty because keeping too little can make useful information unavailable later, while keeping too much imposes costs of its own (keeping-found-things-found research). Irrelevant retained information competes for attention and can obscure material better suited to the current task (keeping-found-things-found research). Capture tools should therefore reduce both false-positive keeps and missed useful information rather than merely make storage cheaper (keeping-found-things-found research).

The broader overload evidence reinforces this boundary because a 2024 scoping review linked information overload to poor decision-making, lower productivity, and cognitive pressure (information-overload review). Overload is not caused by volume alone; the review identifies personal factors, information characteristics, task parameters, organizational parameters, and information-technology parameters (information-overload review). Filtering, prioritization, technology, and multiple skills are among the identified management strategies (information-overload review).

For organizations, selection begins from operating requirements rather than whatever happens to arrive in an inbox because knowledge audits identify what knowledge is needed, available, and used for current activities (knowledge-audit study). Audits also reveal gaps that may limit activity and should be repeated so environmental change can trigger targeted interventions (knowledge-audit study).

Inputs, provisional captures, and durable artifacts

Potential inputs include process needs, observed gaps, source materials, decisions, incidents, expert dependencies, and personal observations because knowledge audits examine needed, available, and used knowledge and expose limiting gaps (knowledge-audit study). A provisional capture can be a bookmark, clip, transcript, screenshot, extracted entity, or AI-produced candidate, but promotion to durable knowledge should depend on expected use and adequate validation because keeping too much creates attention competition (keeping-found-things-found research).

Durable capture should retain the source and the exact target segment where feasible because the W3C Web Annotation model can link arbitrary content to a whole resource or a precise segment, including timed multimedia (Web Annotation). The model was designed to support cross-platform sharing, migration, integration, and reuse without losing significant information (Web Annotation). A context-rich capture should therefore preserve the annotation body, target, selector, creator, time, and transformation path rather than detach a quotation from its origin (Web Annotation).

Personal-data capture must remain limited to the purpose because data minimization requires information to be adequate, relevant, and no more extensive than necessary (ICO data-protection guidance). Held personal data should be reviewed periodically and deleted when it is no longer needed (ICO data-protection guidance).

An eight-part selection and capture workflow

The first step is to restate the task, decision, learning goal, or operational risk that capture should support because knowledge audits work by comparing needed knowledge with what is available and used (knowledge-audit study). The second is to identify demand through process work, recurring failures, questions, and gaps rather than through indiscriminate collection (knowledge-audit study).

The third step is to inventory supply across documents and people, then locate gaps, bottlenecks, and concentrations. APQC describes knowledge mapping as a way to expose critical expertise, gaps, bottlenecks, and concentrated performance risk, but this is practitioner evidence from a blog source (APQC knowledge mapping). ⚠️ The same source says knowledge risk can appear as delays, repeated mistakes, or dependence on a few experts, which is useful operational guidance but remains weak evidence under the report’s grading rule (APQC knowledge mapping). ⚠️

The fourth step is to prioritize candidates by consequence, likelihood of loss, use, and alignment with organizational goals. A case-study framework assessed knowledge-loss risk through likelihood, critical areas, utilization, and strategic alignment and was intended to guide retention or pre-departure capture decisions, but both claims have medium confidence (knowledge-loss framework). ⚠️ These dimensions provide a starting rubric rather than a validated universal score (knowledge-loss framework). ⚠️

The fifth step is to evaluate source credibility through lateral reading. In a comparative study of 45 participants, professional fact-checkers left the focal site after a quick scan and investigated independent sources, reached more warranted conclusions faster than historians and students, and avoided being misled by official-looking logos and domains (lateral-reading study).

The sixth step is to capture the smallest useful unit plus its source segment and context into a staging area, using a source-linked annotation rather than an isolated copy (Web Annotation). The seventh is to validate automated extraction, deduplicate, classify rights, and promote only items that meet the stated purpose because human validation remains necessary where extraction accuracy and entity linking are imperfect (human-in-the-loop workflow). The eighth is to measure later use, misses, corrections, overload, and maintenance cost, then revise selection rules because repeated audits should account for environmental change and trigger interventions (knowledge-audit study).

Personal selection rules and habits

An individual should capture against active questions, projects, decisions, commitments, and learning goals rather than an unlimited imagined future need because excessive keeping creates attention competition and overload (keeping-found-things-found research, information-overload review). A useful item is one that supports a real task, is costly to rediscover, preserves an unrecoverable observation or decision, or supplies a distinctive retrieval cue; low-context replaceable copies should usually remain provisional because wrong information can obscure task-relevant material (keeping-found-things-found research).

A low-friction inbox can reduce missed captures, but it should have an expiry or review window because cheaper keeping also increases false positives and maintenance burden (keeping-found-things-found research). At capture time, record why the item matters and preserve the exact source segment because Web Annotation supports precise targets and interoperable reuse (Web Annotation).

For Web evidence, leave the page to investigate who is behind it and trace important assertions to independent or original sources because professional fact-checkers used that lateral strategy and reached more warranted judgments faster in the cited study (lateral-reading study). Visual polish should not substitute for source credibility because official-looking logos and domain names misled historians and students (lateral-reading study).

Personal-data capture should be limited to what is adequate, relevant, and necessary for the declared purpose, with periodic deletion of material no longer needed (ICO data-protection guidance). A personal capture system should therefore measure later reuse, refinding, clutter, missed important items, source completeness, and expired provisional material rather than celebrate raw capture count (keeping-found-things-found research, Web Annotation).

Organizational critical-knowledge capture

Organizations should make critical-knowledge identification recurring because iterative knowledge audits account for environmental change and trigger informed interventions (knowledge-audit study). The audit should identify needed, available, and used knowledge and reveal gaps that limit current activity (knowledge-audit study).

Risk prioritization can examine likelihood of loss, critical knowledge areas, utilization, and strategic alignment, but the supporting case-study framework is medium confidence and should be adapted rather than copied mechanically (knowledge-loss framework). ⚠️ Decisions about retaining a critical employee or capturing knowledge before departure are one intended use of that framework, not a universal prescription for every departure (knowledge-loss framework). ⚠️

Departing-expert transfer should not rely on digitization alone because a systematic review of 28 studies found that organizations preferred collective approaches to transferring tacit and explicit knowledge (knowledge-transfer review). The review also found that effective procedures were tailored to organizational, sector, and market characteristics (knowledge-transfer review). Documentation, mentoring, observation, and collective work should therefore be combined according to context rather than forced into one generic capture template (knowledge-transfer review).

Meeting, message, and work-telemetry capture must observe purpose limitation and minimization because personal data should be adequate, relevant, and limited to what is necessary (ICO data-protection guidance). Organizations should periodically review those captures and delete personal data that is no longer needed (ICO data-protection guidance).

Architecture and automation patterns

A practical architecture separates discovery, staging, validation, and canonical storage because provisional keeps must remain distinguishable from durable promoted knowledge (keeping-found-things-found research). Discovery can surface gaps from audits and maps, while staging retains candidate captures until relevance, source, rights, and duplication checks are complete (knowledge-audit study, Web Annotation).

Capture adapters should preserve the original source and exact target when feasible because Web Annotation supports arbitrary bodies linked to whole resources, precise data points, or timed multimedia segments (Web Annotation). Its cross-platform design supports migration, integration, and reuse without significant information loss (Web Annotation). Deduplication and entity resolution should propose matches for validation rather than silently merge uncertain records because the human-in-the-loop workflow reports continuing limitations in extraction accuracy and entity linking (human-in-the-loop workflow).

AI can automate extraction and structuring while preserving human oversight through validation, as demonstrated in a 2025 scholarly workflow (human-in-the-loop workflow). ⚠️ That evaluation included only nine specialized participants, so its performance and usability implications are weak and context-specific (human-in-the-loop workflow). ⚠️ The authors nevertheless state with high-confidence evidence that human validation remains essential because extraction accuracy and entity linking still need improvement (human-in-the-loop workflow).
